  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_23482825').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_23482825').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_23482825').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {

<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hi Emily - I know exactly what you mean and I HATE those kind of books (and there's been so many lately!) but I was relieved to find that it wasn't th<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hi Emily - I know exactly what you mean and I HATE those kind of books (and there's been so many lately!) but I was relieved to find that it wasn't the case here. Linus provides support for Audrey, but it takes a lot of effort on her part, the input of her family, and seeing her therapist for her to start getting better. Even by the end of the book, she hasn't made a miraculous recovery and she acknowledges that getting better will be full of ups and downs, as all life generally is.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    From what i understood from the book Audrey only had one true friend in her old school which was Natalie, the other girls which you refer to (Tasha, I<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    From what i understood from the book Audrey only had one true friend in her old school which was Natalie, the other girls which you refer to (Tasha, Izzy etc) were "the Popular" girls in school Tasha being the main one Tasha had even the school faculty wrapped around her finger but one day it went just way to far (the book doesn't give you the story of what happened just details) So when the incident happened the bullies were blamed and kicked out I presume or they just left like izzy did and the trauma from the incident is what gave Audrey her anxiety and fear of contact. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

<div id="review_1304907393" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1304907393" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1304907393?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1304907393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11889029349425644117">Sophie Kinsella used to be such a guilty pleasure author for me. I haven't read one of her books in years but I always enjoyed reading about the hilarious, ridiculous and unfortunate situations her shopaholic protagonist found herself in.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23305614.Finding_Audrey' title='Finding Audrey by Sophie Kinsella' rel='nofollow noopener'>Finding Audrey</a>, though, could be Kinsella's strongest work to date. It's funny, sweet, heartwarming but also - I felt - an honest look at a teenage girl living with social anxiety.<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“They talk about “body language,” as if we all speak it the same. But ever</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText11889029349425644117" style="display:none">Sophie Kinsella used to be such a guilty pleasure author for me. I haven't read one of her books in years but I always enjoyed reading about the hilarious, ridiculous and unfortunate situations her shopaholic protagonist found herself in.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23305614.Finding_Audrey" title="Finding Audrey by Sophie Kinsella" rel="nofollow noopener">Finding Audrey</a>, though, could be Kinsella's strongest work to date. It's funny, sweet, heartwarming but also - I felt - an honest look at a teenage girl living with social anxiety.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“They talk about “body language,” as if we all speak it the same. But everyone has their own dialect. For me right now, for example, swiveling my body right away and staring rigidly at the corner means, “I like you.” Because I didn’t run away and shut myself in the bathroom. I just hope he realizes that.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />One of my favourite things about this book is that it's about one of those families - loud, crazy, often torn apart by arguments, but ultimately very close and loving towards one another. The dynamics Kinsella creates between the members of Audrey's family make this book very funny (and sometimes touching too).<br /><br />Audrey's mother is a neurotic <i>Daily Mail</i> fan who constantly tries to improve her family's lifestyle after reading articles like "The Eight Signs Your Child is Addicted to Computer Games". She's comical, infuriating, but still lovable. Audrey's Dad reluctantly tries to enforce the rules his wife establishes, but he really just wants to keep the peace and watch Downton Abbey. Audrey's older brother Frank is obsessed with a game called LOC (similar to World of Warcraft) and this causes many hilarious arguments with his mum. And then there's Audrey.<br /><br />Audrey is suffering from a severe anxiety disorder. She can hardly bear to leave the house and gets upset whenever Frank's gamer friends come around. However, she does begin to establish a way of communicating through paper notes with one of Frank's friends - Linus. Who, by the way, is so freaking adorable.<br /><br />One of my main concerns when I started this book was that it would turn into another "love cures mental illness" tale. I hate that damaging and untrue message. But, though Linus offers support and friendship to Audrey, the author doesn't allow that message to seep through. Kinsella shows recovery from mental illness as a long process of two steps forward and one step back. Even at the novel's close, Audrey has not been miraculously cured.<br /><br />I liked that. I liked that the book was a good balance of light-hearted silly humour and hard realism. It was really effective.<br /><br />Very enjoyable and touching book.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11889029349425644117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1289103908" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1289103908" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1289103908?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1289103908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6281543170134809796">*** EDIT**** If you don't agree with my opinions on this review, you don't <i>have</i> to comment and tell me I'm wrong. JUST SAYIN'. My opinion isn't going to change.<br/><br/>I want to be very clear about something, though: <b>I didn't finish this book because of ME. It's a book that makes me uncomfortable and unhappy. But that's just <i>me</i>.</b> It's totally a case of "it's you, not me." So YEAH. I don't believe in reading books that make me awfully unhappy. I DNF'd this at 100-pages.<br/><br/><b>This is a book about social anxiety.</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6281543170134809796" style="display:none">*** EDIT**** If you don't agree with my opinions on this review, you don't <i>have</i> to comment and tell me I'm wrong. JUST SAYIN'. My opinion isn't going to change.<br /><br />I want to be very clear about something, though: <b>I didn't finish this book because of ME. It's a book that makes me uncomfortable and unhappy. But that's just <i>me</i>.</b> It's totally a case of "it's you, not me." So YEAH. I don't believe in reading books that make me awfully unhappy. I DNF'd this at 100-pages.<br /><br /><b>This is a book about social anxiety...written in the most insensitive way EVER.</b> It's a joke. The entire book is a <i>joke</i>. I don't know about you, but I can't do that! I can't read a book that mixes something so devastatingly destroying as mental illness with funky writing. As someone with social anxiety, I just feel this book portrayed it as a joke. It is not a joke.<br /><br />This is what went really wrong for me in the 100-pages I read:<br /><br /><b> + The mother is INSANE.</b> Like, kooky har-har-let's-all-laugh-at-the-mother insane. <i>Not okay.</i> We're mixing a real mental illness (Audrey's anxiety) with the mother's kookiness...for a laugh? I couldn't. I JUST COULDN'T. The mother has this huge vendetta against the older brother, Frank's, computer games. No reason. She just is obsessed with making him not play computer games. And I don't mean <i>off-handedly worried</i> I mean, FREAKING OBSESSED. To the point where the parents go out on a "date" and tell Frank he can't play computer games...but secretly the mother is like peering in the window to make sure he doesn't. She falls into a rose bush. Omg, isn't this funny. NO IT IS NOT. Her obsession disturbed me so so much.<br /><b> + Audrey's weird infatuation with Linus.</b> It has a huge case of insta-love. I also think it misses the point that social anxiety is <i>social</i>. Sure people with SAD (Social anxiety disorder) can have crushes, fall in love, get married, everything! But don't forget that your brain is attacking itself and other people are always a threat. I failed to see how this can just be negated by insta-love after seeing someone a few times. (Plus for the level of SAD Audrey "appears" to have, I feel like a relationship would've made her worse. I seriously hope the book didn't do the "magic cure" with a relationship. But I don't know since I didn't finish it because the whole thing made me sick with it's gross misrepresentation.)<br /><br /><b>So as long as you know this is a COMEDY wrapped up with mental illness...you should be okay.</b> I, however, am not. (And seriously, I hate DNF'ing...it makes me twitchy to have unfinished books lying around. So this is a big deal for me.) I think this subject is just too close to home for me laugh at it.<br /><br />If you're looking for books that deal with anxiety in a realistic and heartbreaking and perfect way, and don't mock it <i>at all</i>, can I recommend: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16280081.The_Unlikely_Hero_of_Room_13B" title="The Unlikely Hero of Room 13B by Teresa Toten" rel="nofollow noopener">The Unlikely Hero of Room 13B</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22910900.The_Rest_of_Us_Just_Live_Here" title="The Rest of Us Just Live Here by Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rest of Us Just Live Here</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6281543170134809796" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1947170716" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1947170716" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1947170716?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1947170716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9135222009914046677">I did enjoy my time with this book, but I feel I did not enjoy it as much as my peers. I have had <i>Finding Audrey</i> on my radar for an immensely long time due to it being one of the only YA books I've found to deal with social anxiety, specifically, and while I was pleased with the mental health rep, I found the majority of the rest of the book to be lacking.<br/><br/>The glowing element of this story is absolutely the representation for social anxiety. Audrey is diagnosed with Social Anxiety Disorder and cl</span>
  <span id="freeText9135222009914046677" style="display:none">I did enjoy my time with this book, but I feel I did not enjoy it as much as my peers. I have had <i>Finding Audrey</i> on my radar for an immensely long time due to it being one of the only YA books I've found to deal with social anxiety, specifically, and while I was pleased with the mental health rep, I found the majority of the rest of the book to be lacking.<br /><br />The glowing element of this story is absolutely the representation for social anxiety. Audrey is diagnosed with Social Anxiety Disorder and clinical depression. As someone who has dealt with anxiety and depression for most of my life, I can happily say this book contains an accurate depiction. I love how true of a portrayal this novel is - Social anxiety is not only being afraid to talk on phones, not feeling comfortable in crowds, or having trouble making new friends. It affects all of your interpersonal relationships and makes daily tasks like making eye contact, eating in front of others, or leaving the house almost impossible. <i>(As a note, I've seen a few reviews suggesting Audrey also deals with agoraphobia because she does not leave her home often. As we are given Audrey's official diagnosis in the beginning on the novel and the fact that the fear of leaving her home is not due to a fear of not having an escape in case of disaster but rather her fear of social interaction &amp; judgement from others, I would not consider this book to have representation for agoraphobia, though many who do live with this illness may find some comfort in Audrey's story regardless.)</i> I liked the focus on that an event may have triggered Audrey's anxiety, but it is primarily a chemical imbalance that she has always lived with - it's not only tied to an incident at school. Though this book perfectly displays what it is like to have social anxiety and depression, Audrey is still more than just her illnesses and I feel this book properly showcases the struggle that million of people go through. I also loved that Audrey's treatment was a central theme of the story, and although I'm always unhappy to see YA books demonize the use of medication to treat mental illness, this novel left a strong enough positive message that I can accept it. I've seen a lot of reviews suggest that Audrey recovers "too quickly" which I personally disagree with. I feel this book follows her struggle, her efforts to take control of her anxiety and work past her issues, and ultimate progress. Audrey is in no way "cured" by the end of this novel, she is still struggling despite her improvements and I believe those improvements would be inspiring to make teens in similar situations. If you're looking for a book that deals with social anxiety, I can't recommend <i>Finding Audrey</i> enough.<br /><br />I liked the romance - I don't feel it is anything special, but I was happy to see a supportive love interest that helps the main character in their recovery, yet isn't attributed to as the sole reason they begin to get better. Linus was probably my second favorite character for that reason. I also liked Audrey's brother, Frank, but I don't feel he had a huge contribution to the story. I struggled very hard with Audrey's mother; She is the type of helicopter parent that believes they are doing what is best for their child while simultaneously harming them, and while this is absolutely a real parental role that many teens have to live with, she made the majority of the book extremely unbearable. I don't feel we had enough development on Audrey's father for me to have strong feelings, and apart from being the cute younger brother who acts as comic relief, Felix also isn't a memorable character for me.<br /><br />On the other hand, I didn't love many other aspects of this book. The plot was really lacking - other than it being the story of Audrey dealing with her illnesses, not much happens in this book. I found it very boring at times with a weak driving force. If you are looking for a book with a well-developed plot, I don't believe this is the book for you. I also felt there was too large of a focus on being addicted to video games - At times, it felt as if their mother's obsession with Frank's video game usage overtook the focus on Audrey's story. It wasn't enjoyable and felt gimmicky, making a large portion of the story to be very hard to get through.<br /><br />Additionally, the incident that mostly triggered Audrey's illnesses was never really addressed. We can assume it has something to do with her past classmates and bullying. It is built up to be this huge issue that the school failed to take control of, yet we are never exposed to what it actually is. I understand some authors choose to not include information like this as "the actual event doesn't matter", but it made the book extremely anti-climatic and left me very unsatisfied. It felt lazy and unfinished, I think an actual anecdote about what happened would have strengthened the story.<br /><br />Overall, I'm very pleased I read this book because of the mental health rep, but I can't find any other notable elements of praise. If you're looking for books with social anxiety, I think it's worth giving a shot. If you're not, I'm sure you'd find more enjoyment in a different read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9135222009914046677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2025377958" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2025377958" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2025377958?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family-drama">family-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=social-anxiety">social-anxiety</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2025377958" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3847749104297091734"><b>Sophie Kinsella did it again.</b> <br/><br/>Earlier this week, I read and disliked ELIZA AND HER MONSTERS. I thought it was because the main character was lethargic, which was mostly due to her social anxiety, but so is Audrey. She’s an observer also—very calm, stays inside, interacts little—and I loved the hell out of her voice. <br/>	<br/>Something bad happened to Audrey at her last school, so now she wanders around the house aimlessly. Her doctor tells her to make a video documenting her life, family, recovery, whic</span>
  <span id="freeText3847749104297091734" style="display:none"><b>Sophie Kinsella did it again.</b> <br /><br />Earlier this week, I read and disliked ELIZA AND HER MONSTERS. I thought it was because the main character was lethargic, which was mostly due to her social anxiety, but so is Audrey. She’s an observer also—very calm, stays inside, interacts little—and I loved the hell out of her voice. <br />	<br />Something bad happened to Audrey at her last school, so now she wanders around the house aimlessly. Her doctor tells her to make a video documenting her life, family, recovery, which helps her interact with others and herself. Another new key element in her life is her brother’s new friend to whom she took a liking. <br /><br />I loved the humour. I was so scared it would be similar to WHERE DID YOU GO, BERNADETTE, which is a tragicomedy also, with an isolated protagonist who disappears. But unlike the title suggests, this isn’t a book about the literal definition of finding Audrey. More like the metaphorical one. <br /><br />The characters are very interesting. It revolves around Audrey’s family and Audrey herself. All family members are fully fleshed out, from overly eager little Felix to obsessive stay-at-home Mom. In ELIZA AND HER MONSTERS, Eliza preferred to stay away from her family. She thought of them as an annoyance. I found that extremely irking. Audrey may not necessarily approve of everything her family does—she definitely disfavours the drama—but her affection toward them is obvious to the reader nonetheless. <br /><br />A very addictive novel with entertaining characters and sweet romance. Job well done. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>

<div id="review_1091813179" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1091813179" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1091813179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer192692455833513836"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"Life is all about climbing up, slipping down, and picking yourself up again. And it doesn't matter if you slip down. As long as you're kind of heading more or less upwards. That's all you can hope for. More or less upward."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Sophie Kinsella is on my auto-buy list. Her books are like literary sunshine. They're sweet, heartwarming, and never fail to coax a laugh out of me.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440053212ra/15923832.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Finding Audrey is no exception—with a twist. <br/><br/>The <b>critical reader in me hates it.</b> At the beginning of the book, Audr</span>
  <span id="freeText192692455833513836" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Life is all about climbing up, slipping down, and picking yourself up again. And it doesn't matter if you slip down. As long as you're kind of heading more or less upwards. That's all you can hope for. More or less upward."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Sophie Kinsella is on my auto-buy list. Her books are like literary sunshine. They're sweet, heartwarming, and never fail to coax a laugh out of me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440053212ra/15923832.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Finding Audrey is no exception—with a twist. <br><br>The <b>critical reader in me hates it.</b> At the beginning of the book, Audrey needs to wear sunglasses and can't leave the house because of her anxiety. When a stranger walks into her room, she immediately has a panic attack:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"My chest is starting to rise in panic. Tears have already started to my eyes. My throat feels frozen. I need to escape. I need-- I can't--"</i>
</blockquote><br><br>But halfway through, with no loved ones by her side, she's able to make the 20-minute walk from her house to Starbucks. Busy, bustling Starbucks with its lines and irritable screenplay writers hogging seats.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440053212ra/15923833.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Can you guess how Audrey does it? Yup, you guessed it:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440053212ra/15923834.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Motherfucking love. Because love is the answer to everything. We don't need no food or money as long as we have love! Love can solve mental illness because fuck reality.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440053212ra/15923835.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Now I'm even more mad at this book because it made me look up Justin Bieber gifs.<br><br>Linus, the love interest, feels like a Maniac Pixie Dream Boy. His romantic interest in Audrey has no base. They meet a handful of times in which Audrey flees from him like a startled deer and exchange a few cute notes and then he's utterly head over heels for her. <br><br>Let's be realistic: being in a romantic relationship with a mentally ill person is a lot of work, especially since Audrey's anxiety is quite severe. I'm not saying it's not possible or they don't deserve happily ever afters, but the way it's presented in this book makes me cringe. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18829666.Black_Iris" title="Black Iris by Leah Raeder" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Iris</a> does a fantastic job of charting the highs and lows of falling in love with a bipolar person, while Finding Audrey sugarcoats it.<br><br>That aside, I enjoy the overall message that anxiety is not something that can be footed in a day. It takes time and hard work and often, one step forward results in two steps backward. Kinsella accurately demonstrates how anxiety can weigh on familial relationships, which is lovely.<br><br>Let's not forget the humor:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Dad (Voice-over): A PARTY? Are you serious?<br><br>Mom: Why not? It would be fun. We used to throw him some lovely parties. <br><br>Dad: When he was EIGHT. Anne, do you know what teenage parties are like? What if they knife each other and have sex on the trampoline?</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Basically, my thoughts towards Finding Audrey can be summed up in one Taylor Swift gif:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440053212ra/15923836.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I know I shouldn't, but I love it anyway.<br><br><br><br><b>Pre-review: </b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>An anxiety disorder disrupts fourteen-year-old Audrey’s daily life.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Damn, Kinsella foraying into YA and writing about a serious subject at the same time?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414554202ra/11666780.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="192692455833513836" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1761175050?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24581662-finding-audrey">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=re-reads">re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1761175050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7030936725888457628">So I think my feelings have slightly changed towards this book. The initial fondness or attachment I had isn’t there anymore. <br/><br/>But it was hilarious, it was messy, the parents were irritating beyond belief but I adored them. The social anxiety rep was okay. I did want more focus on it, but I appreciated that we also got to see Audrey in her own messy element, with her family and challenging her social anxiety. <br/><br/><br/>————————<br/><br/>[4.5] This was amaaaazing! I wasn't expecting to actually love it. Just like it </span>
  <span id="freeText7030936725888457628" style="display:none">So I think my feelings have slightly changed towards this book. The initial fondness or attachment I had isn’t there anymore. <br /><br />But it was hilarious, it was messy, the parents were irritating beyond belief but I adored them. The social anxiety rep was okay. I did want more focus on it, but I appreciated that we also got to see Audrey in her own messy element, with her family and challenging her social anxiety. <br /><br /><br />————————<br /><br />[4.5] This was amaaaazing! I wasn't expecting to actually love it. Just like it more or less. But I couldn't help but actually fall in love with this book. <br /><br />In true Kinsella style, it was hilarious! Throughout the whole book I was actually laughing out loud to myself. Way too many times. I loved the family. They were genuine, real, supportive and a mess. <br /><br />The main character suffers from social anxiety and it follows her journey of trying to overcome it. I loved the overall message, the writing and in general, the whole story. We get to see the protagonist progress but also suffer from a few setbacks and learning to deal with her situation. <br /><br />I wish there was more. More development to the anxiety Audrey deals with, the story and the characters, but it does make for a lighthearted read with a message. <br /><br />Definitely recommend this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7030936725888457628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1668185931" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1668185931" />
    <a title="Ryan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56788355-ryan"><img alt="Ryan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468129599p2/56788355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1668185931?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan" href="/user/show/56788355-ryan">Ryan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56788355-ryan?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56788355-ryan?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56788355-ryan?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56788355-ryan?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56788355-ryan?shelf=september-tbr">september-tbr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56788355-ryan?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56788355-ryan?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1668185931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14559655251962729492"><b>
  <i>"The trouble is, depression doesn't come with handy symptoms like spots and a temperature, so you don't realize it at first. You keep saying "I'm fine" to people when you're not fine. You think you should be fine. You keep saying to yourself: "Why aren't I fine?"</i>
</b><br/><br/>This is going to be one long-ass review, everyone.<br/><br/>Let me just preface this by saying one reason why I love this book so much is because of how personal the topic is to me. Some of this review will be a ramble-y description of my expe</span>
  <span id="freeText14559655251962729492" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"The trouble is, depression doesn't come with handy symptoms like spots and a temperature, so you don't realize it at first. You keep saying "I'm fine" to people when you're not fine. You think you should be fine. You keep saying to yourself: "Why aren't I fine?"</i>
</b><br><br>This is going to be one long-ass review, everyone.<br><br>Let me just preface this by saying one reason why I love this book so much is because of how personal the topic is to me. Some of this review will be a ramble-y description of my experiences with anxiety (which I will put in a spoiler tag at the very end). <br><br><b><i>"To put you out of your misery, here's the full diagnosis: Social Anxiety Disorder, General Anxiety Disorder, and Depressive Episodes.</i><br>Episodes. <i>Like depression is a sitcom with a fun punch line each time. Or a TV box set loaded with cliffhangers. The only cliffhanger in my life is</i> "Will I ever get rid of this shit?" <i>and believe me, it gets pretty monotonous.</i></b><br><br>Finding Audrey is a book that I didn't expect to love as much as I did. I was expecting a typical mental illness contemporary, where the MC has something "wrong" with them, meets some love interest, is miraculously cured, and then goes to make-out or have sex, or whatever the fuck with their insta-lover. <b>This was nothing like that.</b> This was a humourous, hard-hitting story about the realities of living with a mental illness. Not the romanticized, bullshit versions authors keep putting out. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474177744ra/20563971.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Can we just take a moment to appreciate the accurate portrayal of anxiety and mental illness here? Like:<br><br><b>
  <i>"Eye contact is a big deal. It's the biggest deal. Just the thought makes me sick, right down to my core.<br>I know in my rational head that that eyes are not frightening. They're tiny little harmless blobs of jelly. They're, like, a minuscule fraction of our whole body area. We all have them. So why should they bother me? But I've had a lot of time to think about this, and if you ask me, most people underestimate eyes. For a start, they're powerful...They're like vortexes, too. They're infinite. You look someone straight in the eye and your whole soul can be sucked out in a nanosecond. That's what it feels like. Other people's eyes are limitless and that's what scares me."</i>
</b><br><br>And:<br><br><b><i>"It's all my fault, my stupid,</i> stupid <i>fault...<br>My thoughts are speeding up and my pace is speeding up too, and I'm pulling at my arms, pulling at the flesh of my forearms, trying to...I don't know.. I don't understand it. I glance in the mirror and flinch at my own wild stare. I can feel a weird sparking all over my body, like I'm more alive than I should be, like my body is</i> over-loaded <i>with life force. Can you have too much life stuffed into one body? Because that's what this feels like. And everything's too fast. My heart, my thoughts, my feet, my clawing arms..."</i></b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474176039ra/20563840.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I applaud you, Sophie Kinsella.<br><br><b>
  <i>"I'll do anything. I'll stack the dishwasher. I'll phone Grandma every night. I'll..." He casts wildly about. "I'll read to deaf people."<br>Read to deaf people? Can he actually hear what he's saying?"</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409788334ra/11022499.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even though this book deals with such a heavy topic, it is still incredibly funny. I'm a fairly easy person to make laugh, so I don't know how credible my word is, but I found this book nothing short of hilarious.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474176039ra/20563841.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><i>"Parents have this way of asking really dumb, obvious questions.</i><br>Are you going out in that skirt?<i><br>No, I'm planning to take it off as soon as I get out of the front door.</i><br>Do you think that's a good idea?<i><br>No, I think it's a terrible idea, that's why I'm doing it.</i><br>Are you listening to me?<i><br>Your voice is a hundred decibels, I can hardly avoid it."</i></b><br><br>Audrey's family is another thing I loved. Her anti-video game mom, her lovably naive little brother, her clueless father, and her video game obsessed brother were absolutely wonderful. Not only in their endless support of Audrey, but in their dynamic. They seemed like a real family. Hell, they kind of seemed like my family, and in more ways than one.<br><br><b>
  <i>"I've gone up a level. That's the only way I can describe it. (...) Yes, I've had one bad episode, but I didn't sink quite as low. Things weren't quite as dark."</i>
</b><br><br>Linus and Audrey <b>*fangirls*</b> They're so fucking cute. I loved how Linus wasn't the cure-all end-all to Audrey's anxiety. Sure, he helped a bit, but meeting him didn't "save her life." She helped herself, with the aid of her family and therapist. Even in the end, Audrey's not 100% fine, <b>and that's okay.</b> No one's fine, really, if you think about it. After all, <b><i>"I'm not okay, you're not okay, and that's okay."</i> - Elisabeth Kubler-Ross</b><br><br><b>
  <i>"I guess Mum was right about the jagged graphs thing. We're all on one. Even Frank. Even Mum. Even Felix. I think what I've realized is, life is all about climbing up, slipping down, and picking yourself up again. And it doesn't matter if you slip down. As long as you're kind of heading more or less upwards. That's all that you can hope for. More or less upwards."</i>
</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(This could possibly be very soppy and cliche, but what else would you expect from me?)<br><br>My experience with anxiety: <br><br>This is probably the easiest and hardest thing I've ever had to write. Easy, I know exactly what I want to write. Hard, because what I want to write involves sharing a very personal part of my life with hundreds of strangers on the Internet. <b>So.</b> Here goes nothing:<br><br>When I was very little, I was one of the shyest kids out there. I wouldn't talk much to new people. I was the kid sitting quietly on the swings, book in hand, while the other kids my age ran around the playground, screaming and yelling at the top of their lungs. It wasn't until I started Preschool that I was able to break out of my shell. From that day on, <i>I</i> was the one of the loud kids. I was friends with everyone. I preformed in my city's theatre program. I dreamed of one day becoming a singer and auditioning for <i>America's Got Talent</i>. I wanted to <i>do</i> everything, <i>see</i> everything.<br><br>But despite all of that, I was a very anxious kid. Overly-anxious. No one really noticed then - I didn't even notice myself. But I can remember all of my irrational fears, how long it would take me to calm down once I was scared, and how the smallest, most insignificant things would affect me greatly.<br><br>This never really became a problem until I was 13. Things happened to me. Not horrid, awful things, but things that impacted me enough to make me revert back to my old ways. My grandpa died. My dad moved out. My grades started slipping. People that I thought were my friends quickly turned on me. <br><br>I remember my first panic attack like most would remember their first kiss. I couldn't breathe, I couldn't think, I couldn't speak. All I could do was sit there, shaking, as tears streamed down my face, and my heart pounded in my ears, and my breath came in shallow gasps. I didn't know what was happening to me. I though I was dying. (But, then again, every time I felt even remotely under the weather, I thought I was dying.) <br><br>Somehow, it passed. I tried to move on, but I couldn't get that day out of my mind. <br><br>Slowly, after a while, I began to experience these things more often. I retreated from the world, and I had started to go out less and less. I developed a fear of cameras, airplanes, social media, spiders, germs, the ocean, people - you name a fear, and chances are, I probably had it. I started to cover all of my cameras with tape. I couldn't look people in the eyes when I spoke to them. I didn't leave the house for weeks, sometimes months on end. Panic attacks became a regular thing, and it wasn't uncommon for me to have one once, twice, maybe even three times a week. I was seeing a therapist, but that wasn't doing much. I didn't <i>want</i> to get better. I wanted to hide. Sometimes, on very bad days, I thought the world would be better off without me. <br><br>During all of this, reading was my only solace. Books weren't judgmental. Books didn't turn on you. They contained whole worlds for me to run to.<br><br>I continued living like this for years, until only recently - when I stumbled upon this little site called Goodreads. <br><br>A social media platform for people <i>who loved books.</i> This sounded like an actual paradise to me. I had to join. The only problem was, that involved starting an account. A <i>social media account</i>. Something I had avoided like the plague for years. Just the thought made my heart beat faster, and my breath catch. <br><br>But I was tired of living like this, scared of everything, and everyone. I clicked "sign-up." At first, I vowed to only use my account to find new books. I wouldn't comment anything, I wouldn't follow anyone. And I sure as <i>hell</i> wasn't going to friend anyone.<br><br>That worked for maybe two weeks. One day, out of the blue, I got two friend requests. I was so taken aback, I shut off my laptop, and had a mini-panic attack in the corner of my room. But my therapist was always telling me to take small risks, and to broaden my horizons. So I accepted the friend requests. I started commenting things. I started reviewing books. <br><br>This progress wasn't just limited to my online life. I started going out more. I started talking to new people. I had some bad episodes, yes, and I had some minor setbacks, but I wasn't going to let that stop me. <br><br>Just recently, I uncovered my phone's back camera. Then the front camera. And holy shit, did it scare me. But it thrilled me, too. I did it. I looked a camera in the eye and said, "I'm not afraid of you."<br><br>Even now, with all the progress I've made, I'm not fully cured. I still have trouble maintaining eye contact. My laptop camera is still covered. I still haven't really gone "out" out. A week ago, I had one of the worst panic attacks I've had in months. But afterwards, I didn't feel so bad. I got back up. I'm on a jagged graph myself, just like Audrey.<br><br>I owe a lot to the first two people who friend requested me (I can't even remember their names, and honestly, I feel terrible about it.) Even though they didn't know it, they gave me that little push I needed to start again.<br><br><b>If any of you are in the same, or similar boat as me, do not be afraid to message me. I know it's scary talking to a complete stranger about your problems. But it may make you feel better. It did for me.</b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="14559655251962729492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2368773410" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2368773410" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2368773410?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2368773410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15968028394597879992">this was, like, the weirdest ever.<br/><br/>who knew that sophie kinsella would write YA? who knew that sophie kinsella would write YA, and then it would follow a 14-year-old girl suffering from immense social anxiety?<br/><br/>one thing we did know, though, is that if sophie kinsella were to write a YA contemporary it would, of course, have a massive romance. that goes without saying.<br/><br/>i liked the mental health rep in this a lot. it was everything else that was kind of meh for me. the romance was very insta-love-y, </span>
  <span id="freeText15968028394597879992" style="display:none">this was, like, the weirdest ever.<br /><br />who knew that sophie kinsella would write YA? who knew that sophie kinsella would write YA, and then it would follow a 14-year-old girl suffering from immense social anxiety?<br /><br />one thing we did know, though, is that if sophie kinsella were to write a YA contemporary it would, of course, have a massive romance. that goes without saying.<br /><br />i liked the mental health rep in this a lot. it was everything else that was kind of meh for me. the romance was very insta-love-y, and almost...manic pixie dream <i>boy</i>? like this kid linus comes in from out of nowhere and is very flat and we know very little about him and then he just HEALS audrey and like. that's it. she has a bit of a flare up but that's it, and everything is very quickly wonderful. <br /><br />so audrey has social anxiety, right, and she wears dark sunglasses pretty much all the time in order to avoid eye contact. and linus, boy wonder/boyfriend of the year, is like. "just take them off!" and she's like, it's not that simple. (which, good. in real life it's not.) and he's like, can't it be that simple if you want it to? and she's all, no. (correct answer.) but then by the end of the book it's like wait actually?? yes.<br /><br />is any of this making sense? i'm full on rambling. <br /><br />anyway. the family was very cartoonish (obsessive mom, out of it dad, very very childish four year old brother, video game-obsessed elder brother). the whole thing felt very disconnected, like a series of vignettes? it was really short and weird.<br /><br />bottom line: i liked audrey's voice. i liked the mental health rep. everything else FAILED THOSE TWO THINGS IMMENSELY.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15968028394597879992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1586743127" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1586743127" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1586743127?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/46791746-ricah-vamptimesurfer">Ricah (vamptimesurfer)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=lol">lol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=somebody-s-sick">somebody-s-sick</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=easy-read">easy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1586743127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer810220852066188889"><br/><b>Adorable alert! </b> And I’m not even talking about the romance because although there may be a little romance, it’s not really romance-romance. It’s still more about friendship. You’ll understand what I mean (although I still would have better appreciated it had the main characters been a bit older) when you read the book.<br/><br/> The novel made me laugh so much from the first page till the very end. I enjoyed everything about it which is a wonderful surprise because this is a story about a girl <b>(Audrey)</b> d</span>
  <span id="freeText810220852066188889" style="display:none"><br /><b>Adorable alert! </b> And I’m not even talking about the romance because although there may be a little romance, it’s not really romance-romance. It’s still more about friendship. You’ll understand what I mean (although I still would have better appreciated it had the main characters been a bit older) when you read the book.<br /><br /> The novel made me laugh so much from the first page till the very end. I enjoyed everything about it which is a wonderful surprise because this is a story about a girl <b>(Audrey)</b> diagnosed with SAD aka Social Anxiety Disorder and it’s supposed to be depressing or just sad but because the story focuses on how Audrey conquers her depression which becomes less of a challenge everyday with a loving (even though chaotic), hilarious family and a very helpful, cute boy called <b>Linus</b> behind her every step of the way, the overall tone of the story is really light and comfy and the message very inspiring too. The creative writing format is also a huge contributor to the overall bright and positive impact of the novel. <br /><br /> More than anything, it’s the perfect picture of a regular mess of a family (complete with a 14 year old queen of overreaction who always wears a pair of dark glasses, a computer game 15 year old addict but a real genius called <b>Frank,</b> the cutest, fluffy four year old boy <b>Felix,</b> a loud, overly involved, <b>hyper mom</b> and a handsome but <b>comic dad</b> who always agrees with the hyper mom) that I loved the most about the novel. <b> Stereotypes much? Maybe, but they don’t make the story less true!</b><br /><br /> This is too cute! The contemporary references, the hilarious parent-child confrontations/battles, everything is just so current and spot on! <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6160.Sophie_Kinsella" title="Sophie Kinsella" rel="nofollow noopener">Sophie Kinsella</a> is an expert on teenagers and the crises that both parents and teens confront during this formidable stage in a person’s life. You can’t help but adore the way the subject was tackled and how it impresses upon the reader that everyone goes through a state of depression. But as in any case, we have a choice and when our choices are steered by how they will affect the people we love, we’re usually guaranteed to choose for the better. <br /><br /><u>Quote highlight:</u><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Eyes are like vortexes. They’re infinite. You look someone straight in the eye and your whole soul can be sucked out in a nano-second.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Thanks to my young and sweet friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/46791746-ricah" rel="nofollow noopener">Ricah</a> for her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1412911212?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">lovely review</a> that inspired me to read the book. Also, happy birthday, young one! Enjoy your special day! &lt;3<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="810220852066188889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1122596720" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1122596720" />
    <a title="April (Aprilius Maximus)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus"><img alt="April (Aprilius Maximus)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589331862p2/20658145.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1122596720?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="April (Aprilius Maximus)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="April (Aprilius Maximus)" href="/user/show/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus">April (Aprilius Maximus)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780857534590" href="/book/show/23482825-finding-audrey">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1122596720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8354999794589167680">Watch my video review or read on for the written review :) <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4mD7VF5jQts'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4mD7V...</a><br/>Thank you so much to Doubleday Children's for sending me this book! <br/>I have a lot of mixed feelings about this book! At first I was so excited for it because it sounded perfect for me because when I was Audrey's age, I had actually gone through something freakishly similar to her in this book! But then again, I had issues with it that I was hoping wouldn't arise but unfortunately I couldn't ignore. </span>
  <span id="freeText8354999794589167680" style="display:none">Watch my video review or read on for the written review :) <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4mD7VF5jQts">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4mD7V...</a><br />Thank you so much to Doubleday Children's for sending me this book! <br />I have a lot of mixed feelings about this book! At first I was so excited for it because it sounded perfect for me because when I was Audrey's age, I had actually gone through something freakishly similar to her in this book! But then again, I had issues with it that I was hoping wouldn't arise but unfortunately I couldn't ignore. <br />I'll start off by saying that a lot of things about Audrey and this book were so similar to me that I was freaking out a little bit. Like, Sophie Kinsella, did you steal my diary from when I was 14 or what? When I was 14, I was bullied and had a really rough time in high school, so much so that I couldn't go to school, or even leave my own house (all of which happens to Audrey). I also developed a relationship with a boy who helped me greatly and moved schools (like Audrey plans to do). IS THAT NOT FREAKY? <br />Anyway, Sophie Kinsella's writing style is great because it reads like one of those comedy tv shows and it also contains film scripts and notes that speed up and enhance the reading experience! <br />Moving on to the many things that I had issues with:<br /> - The fact that you never find out what happened in detail to cause her anxiety to dictate her mind.<br /> - The unrealistic and stereotyped parental figures. Her mother was the typical "video games are bad for you and you need to play outside because that's what I did when I was younger" except exaggerated TIMES A THOUSAND. Her father was a classic 'always on his blackberry and never hears what his wife says and just agrees with everything she says' kinda guy and I found them to be REALLY unrealistic. I mean, I'm sure there are parents out there that are like this, but to the extent where I found myself questioning how exaggerated these stereotypes were was ridiculous. <br /> - The insta-love. Now, I understand that at Audrey's age, you get into a relationship and you're telling each other you love them straight away (I know, because I did that too. Oh how silly I was!) but I thought it was a bit strange that one minute Audrey was having such bad anxiety that she couldn't look him in the eye or even face him and the next minute they're making out? It just didn't make that much sense to me, especially coming from someone who has experienced severe anxiety at that age and throughout my entire life.<br /><br />It had its cute moments but I wouldn't recommend it. I really wish I could have loved it :(</span>
  <a data-text-id="8354999794589167680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1384970202" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1384970202" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1384970202?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1384970202&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1384970202" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12266153527968774438">I'm impressed with how much I enjoyed this! I've heard so much praise about Sophie Kinsella's writing, and I adored it! It's very reminiscent of The Fault in our Stars with the entire sassy "omg whatever" teenager type narration, a sarcastic YA trope that I thought I was hate but ended up actually chuckling at a couple of times. The characters in this book were phenomenal. Audrey's family is hilarious and every character was so well-written and real; I adored them all even though everyone had th</span>
  <span id="freeText12266153527968774438" style="display:none">I'm impressed with how much I enjoyed this! I've heard so much praise about Sophie Kinsella's writing, and I adored it! It's very reminiscent of The Fault in our Stars with the entire sassy "omg whatever" teenager type narration, a sarcastic YA trope that I thought I was hate but ended up actually chuckling at a couple of times. The characters in this book were phenomenal. Audrey's family is hilarious and every character was so well-written and real; I adored them all even though everyone had their own quirks! But Audrey's anxiety disorder rubbed me the wrong way. The book says that a certain event at school triggered it, but it never told us what that event was. There was a huge build-up and never a reveal of what happened. The aftermath was so severe, I'm having trouble putting together the pieces of what happened. Furthermore, I'm baffled that she is able to recover so quickly and spontaneously as soon as she and Linus become friends. I've heard people complain about this book saying anxiety can't be fixed by a relationship, and I have to agree. I think her recovery was too quick-- and the pace of this book just went too fast in general; there was a very unrealistic jump from "omg don't enter the same room as me" to "omg let's make out." <br />I'm just left confused because i'm not entirely sure what disorder she had, why, and how she was able to recover so quickly. Nevertheless, I'm excited to try other Sophie Kinsella books that don't butcher mental health issues.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9242282627080659793">The story is about Audrey who suffers from Social Anxiety Disorder.   <span id="freeText9242282627080659793" style="display:none">The story is about Audrey who suffers from Social Anxiety Disorder. Audrey is convalescing at home after a particularly bad episode brought on by some bullying at school when Linus enters her life and helps to drag her out of her cage.<br /><br />At least, that’s what the blurb would have you think. But the truth is it’s Audrey, her doctor and a bit of prodding from Linus that really sees Audrey on the path to recovery – and for someone who keeps dark glasses on and can’t stand to speak to anyone outside her family, that path is very, very steep.<br /><br />Where this book really shines is Audrey’s family and their day-to-day interactions. Believe me when I say they are hysterically funny and add a much needed character and charm to the story.<br /><br />It’s heartwarming, sweet and very readable with good writing and a solidly paced story.<br /><br />Get into it, people!<br /><br />This is just a short review since I did a video review of it. But I'm not going to tell you where because it's horrible. </span>
