<div id="review_1891230768" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1891230768" />
    <a title="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63164992-grace-burtsbooks"><img alt="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517623708p2/63164992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1891230768?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" href="/user/show/63164992-grace-burtsbooks">Grace (BURTSBOOKS)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780857534590" href="/book/show/23482825-finding-audrey">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63164992-grace-burtsbooks?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1891230768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10169908448911112198">This is the worst book I’ve ever read. <br/><br/>Okay, objectively I know that I’ve read much worse books. The writing and plot of this book are not the worst I’ve ever read and it’s readable unlike some other books I’ve read but I didn’t hate those as much as I hate this. I hate this book. And yes, I know hate is a strong word and I shouldn’t waste my energy on hating a book when that energy could go to reading books that I will end up loving but this book hurt me. This book offended me so deeply and the</span>
  <span id="freeText10169908448911112198" style="display:none">This is the worst book I’ve ever read. <br /><br />Okay, objectively I know that I’ve read much worse books. The writing and plot of this book are not the worst I’ve ever read and it’s readable unlike some other books I’ve read but I didn’t hate those as much as I hate this. I hate this book. And yes, I know hate is a strong word and I shouldn’t waste my energy on hating a book when that energy could go to reading books that I will end up loving but this book hurt me. This book offended me so deeply and there’s no other word to use. I hate it. I hate the way it’s made me feel. <br /><br />Finding Audrey is about a girl who is so crippled by her anxiety that she can’t leave her house. She hasn’t been to school in months because of extenuating circumstances, hasn’t talked to any of her classmates or friends, can’t even look her family members in the eye… until she meets her brother’s friend, Linus and then she magically gets better…. Or something. <br /><br />I really thought I was going to relate to this book. <br /><br />Tragically, I was recommended this book by my therapist, who I was seeing for anxiety…. So, yeah, I was expecting this book to be good rep and hopefully give me some sort of comfort and a story to look to for hope when my anxiety got the best of me. I didn’t get that. This book is a sorry excuse for representation and I can not believe how atrociously the author handled this topic. <br /><br />I think it goes without saying that the ‘boy fixes girl’ trope is over done and highly problematic and just unrealistic. Not to mention in this book it makes absolutely no sense. It all happens so fast; you can’t even call what Audrey goes through development. The plot progression is stilted and the character development suffers because of it. For example, one minute, Audrey can’t talk to Linus at all, doesn’t want him in the house and has to write notes in order to speak to him and the next they’re making out. I’m not joking, on the same exact page she can’t look at him and then one paragraph later they are swapping spit. Or, she can’t leave the house and then she’s going to Starbucks. Granted she does panic over this. The whole way to Starbucks she’s panicking and then we get to Starbucks and she can easily talk to the barista without so much as a batted eye…. I don’t get it. Or even better, Linus tells her to go talk to random people at Starbucks and she just does it…? And then feels better afterwards and can do it again and again. I’m sorry but that’s not how anxiety works. Just because you manage to do something that causes you anxiety once doesn’t mean the anxiety goes away the next time you try to do it… it’s always there and portraying it as this thing that can be so easily overcome is really insensitive. <br /><br />Not to mention, we don’t get to know Linus at all. I’m not kidding, I couldn’t even tell you if he has any siblings. All we know is that he plays video games and he’s Audrey’s brothers friend. His literal only purpose is to “fix” Audrey. He’s only there to kiss her and tell her to talk to random people and congratulations, she’s cured. <br /><br />I really don’t understand why people like this book…. Not only is it terrible representation, it’s just not interesting and the writing is bland. Yes, this is just my opinion and you can like what you like but why? <br /><br />So yeah. I wish I never read this book. Even though I understand that this book is unrealistic and wrong, it really pains me that a lot of people younger than me will go into this book expecting representation and a form of hope and come out with 1) an unrealistic expectation that one person can cure you 2) an even more unrealistic expectation that recovery will be fast and seamless. <br /><br />This is just so so wrong. 1) Romance is already so toxic in a lot of media forms and the idea that a romantic interest (in this case, like most cases, a man) can fix something as ingrained as anxiety is a terrifying and damaging idea to be perpetuating to young girls. 2) Anxiety, like all mental illness, is life long struggle and it doesn’t just go away. Our anxieties will always be there, they are a part of life but as we recover, we learn how to deal with our anxieties more and I wish YA authors understood this better. Just once I want a book about a realistic recovery. I want to read about a character learning how to live their best life and learning ways to deal with their mental illness in healthy and careful ways… I don’t want to read about someone being fixed by some dude. I want them to learn how to help themselves and in turn help readers learn to help themselves.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10169908448911112198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4308825974777466297" style="display:none">Finding Audrey, Sophie Kinsella<br /><br />An anxiety disorder disrupts fourteen-year-old Audrey's daily life. She has been making slow but steady progress with Dr. Sarah, but when Audrey meets Linus, her brother's gaming teammate, she is energized. <br /><br />She connects with him. Audrey can talk through her fears with Linus in a way she's never been able to do with anyone before. As their friendship deepens and her recovery gains momentum, a sweet romantic connection develops, one that helps not just Audrey but also her entire family.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز هفتم ماه آگوست سال 2018 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: در جست‌و‌جوی آدری‏؛ نویسنده سوفی کینسلا‬‏‫؛ مترجم: سپیده پوراکبر‬‏‫؛ ویراستار نسیم بذرافشان؛ تهران‏‫: ابوعطا، کتاب‌های بادبادک‏‫، 1396؛ در 344ص؛ شابک 9786001702870؛ چاپ دوم 1397؛ موضوع: ‬داستانهای نویسندگان بریتانیایی - سذه 21م<br /><br />در جستجوی آدری؛ با طنزی هنرمندانه، دلبستگی، و بهبود شرایط روانی شخصیت اصلی داستان را، به تصویر میکشد، به نحویکه میتواند برای تمامی خوانشگران الهامبخش و سرگرم کننده باشد.؛ «آدری» دختریست چهارده ساله، که اختلال اضطراب، زندگی روزمره ی او را، مختل کرده است.؛ او به یاری روانپزشک خویش، «دکتر سارا»، پیشرفتی آهسته، ولی پیوسته، به سوی بهبودی داشته است، ولی وقتی با «لینوس»، دوست برادرش، دیدار میکند، این پیشرفت دوچندان میشود.؛ «آدری» میتواند در مورد ترسهایش به «لینوس» بگوید، و او را در جریان مشکلات خویش بگذارد.؛ راهکارهایی که «لینوس» به منظور مواجهه با ترس، در اختیار «آدری» میگذارد، سبب میشود روند بهبود او سرعت بیشتری پیدا کرده، و او بتواند گام به گام از محدوده ی امن خود خارج شده، و با دنیای خارج، که روزی برای او بسیار مخوف و هراسناک بود، ارتباط برقرار کند<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 29/05/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_1226623371" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1226623371" />
    <a title="Irena BookDustMagic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17737927-irena-bookdustmagic"><img alt="Irena BookDustMagic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362943196p2/17737927.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1226623371?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irena BookDustMagic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irena BookDustMagic" href="/user/show/17737927-irena-bookdustmagic">Irena BookDustMagic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1226623371" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12504887256972349863"><b>4,5 stars!</b><br/><br/>Once again, Sophie Kinsella reminded me why am I still so in love with reading books.<br/>If you didn't know, Kinsella is the one who got me into reading in the first place. With her Shopaholic series she showed me reading can be fun and now, years after reading her first book, I still enjoy spending my free time with a good book in my hands (or on my Kindle).<br/><br/>When I first heard she was about to publish a novel in my favorite genre, I just knew I had to read it immediately.<br/><b>I had a great feel</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12504887256972349863" style="display:none"><b>4,5 stars!</b><br /><br />Once again, Sophie Kinsella reminded me why am I still so in love with reading books.<br />If you didn't know, Kinsella is the one who got me into reading in the first place. With her Shopaholic series she showed me reading can be fun and now, years after reading her first book, I still enjoy spending my free time with a good book in my hands (or on my Kindle).<br /><br />When I first heard she was about to publish a novel in my favorite genre, I just knew I had to read it immediately.<br /><b>I had a great feeling about Finding Audrey and I was not wrong.</b><br /><br />In her recognizable style that consists humor, Kinsella writes about serious topics such as anxiety and abusement.<br />I imagine it must have been hard work to touch those serious topics and stay true to her writing style without overdoing the fun parts and diverge from the direction the story was going to. She managed it very well.<br /><br /><b>Audrey</b>, our main character, was a great narrator. She talked about her problems not quite openly but opened herself one step at the time trough the story. I liked that a lot. Even though she had some serious things on her way, it didn't suppress her sense of humor.<br />I think the reason she was hiding behind the dark glasses was justified and I liked that part about her.<br /><br />What I liked the most in this story were <b>Audrey's parents</b>. They were like a fresh scent in the air in the YA genre which is full of dysfunctional families.<br /><br /><b>Frank</b> was my favorite. I liked his obsession with video games and his adaptability when it comes to playing them.<br /><br /><b>Linus</b> was an okay character. Very patient and likeable but I wish there were just something more about him that would make him more distinguish from all of love interests I was reading about in other books. I feel like I'm still missing that final touch that would make him get under my skin.<br /><br />I also wish there were more situations with <b>Felix</b>.<br /><br />The reason I didn't give this book a full five star rating is (HERE COMES THE SPOILER PART) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[we never found out what really happened that triggered Audrey's anxiety.<br />I also didn't like the fact that Audrey got herself off the medications by herself. It is something not anyone should ever do, and in the real life the consequences could be really bad (trust me, I know). I just hope that someone who's on medications while reading this book won't find the courage to do the same thing because Audrey did it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>If you like Sophie Kinsella's previous work, and if you like YA genre, you will (probably) definitely like this book.<br /><br />It was a quick, easy read, perfect to read in one sitting for those who actually can read the book in one sitting.<br /><br />I wish you all A-GREAT-TIME reading it!! :)</b><br /><br /><br /><i>I got a copy of this book via Netgalley for free in an exchange for an honest review. Thank you Penguin Random House UK Children's.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12504887256972349863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1313045215?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=likeable-mc">likeable-mc</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1313045215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17828827372849287059"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437533383i/15595825._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Okay, first : <b>I love Kinsella's works</b> (thought it was important to <s>say</s> write). Now, her books are the first ones I read in English, so, you know, I might need to reread them some day (I mean duh. I'm not a language snowflake). Anyway : Kinsella? She gets my humor. I mean not me <i>me</i>, but you get it right? Her books make me laugh. They're refreshing. Like candies. Okay, maybe not like candies - Well, let's say that they put me in the <i>Kinsella bubble</i>. <br/><br/>What is it? Just look, it's just like <b>life</b>, but </span>
  <span id="freeText17828827372849287059" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437533383i/15595825._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay, first : <b>I love Kinsella's works</b> (thought it was important to <s>say</s> write). Now, her books are the first ones I read in English, so, you know, I might need to reread them some day (I mean duh. I'm not a language snowflake). Anyway : Kinsella? She gets my humor. I mean not me <i>me</i>, but you get it right? Her books make me laugh. They're refreshing. Like candies. Okay, maybe not like candies - Well, let's say that they put me in the <i>Kinsella bubble</i>. <br><br>What is it? Just look, it's just like <b>life</b>, but it's <i>fun</i> : <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437533383i/15595826._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Because what I love even more in them is <b>the undercurrent of reality they hide behind the laughs</b>. This is something that works for me, because I'm not (well, rarely) a full-angst girl. I just can't. I read a book filled with angst and I just want to bang my head on the wall you know? So, Kinsella? Perfect. I know that some readers found shocking that she could deal with such a heavy issue - Audrey's anxiety disorder - in a funny way. I'm not, not one bit, because it stays respectful. <b>Full of empathy. Honest. <i>True</i></b>. And it shows something that I find necessary : people aren't their disorder. They're not entirely defined by it. Yes, <u>it's important</u>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437533383i/15595827._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Audrey suffers from an anxiety disorder : she can neither leave the house nor stare into people's eyes. Actually I'm with her on this : eyes scare me too. I mean, she does have a point : when you look carefully at people you give them the power and the means to stare back. I hate when strangers stare right into my eyes. I'm not shy or anxious. My eyes are just my personal space. Leave it. I also hate when people I don't know touch me. Like for real. Did you need to touch my arm to ask me what time is it? Hell no you didn't. It's not that I don't like people - I'm comfortable enough - but I like my personal space <i>more</i>. Anyway. Audrey. I loved her. <b>She was witty, realistic and relatable</b>. She made me laugh and yeah, tear out a bit at some point. <b>Even if it's not always easy, she <i>fights</i>, she never gives up and I loved that about her.</b> For me, she's <i>brave</i>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437533383i/15595828._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>► It's not a secret that <b>I love family dynamics when they're done well</b>. SPOILER ALERT : They are. Every member of the family is flawed but so endearing and supportive, I spent such a great time following them. <br><br>● Felix made me miss my Kindergarten teaching years : 4 years old is such a great age. Really. They're happy all the time (except when they're not, but then, it's short). <br><br>● Frank the gamer : I feel you. Go explain to people that no, gaming doesn't make you crazy. Sigh. He completely won me with his witty comments. <br><br>● By the way, I'm <i>so</i> going to throw this book at my mum. Yes, kindly (is that what you think of me? Come on). Indeed Audrey's mum Daily Mail obsession cracked me up, and yes, I can relate. Here's how our mother-daughter phone calls go : <br><br><b>Mum</b> : Have you bought curcuma/vitamines/royal jelly/magical product as I told you? <br><b>Anna</b> : [awkward silence when I try to remember why the fuck I'm supposed to buy that] Hmm not yet (I mean, come on) <br><b>Mum</b> : But you need it! There's plenty of [add some information about how it's gonna boost my health] in it. I saw this [show/paper/documentary] the other day and [add some descriptions about how freaking amazing this stuff is]<br><b>Anna</b> : Okay. I'll do it. (not really)<br><br><i>Two days later</i><br><br><b>Mum</b> : Have you bought [add magical product sub-mentioned] as I told you?<br><b>Anna</b> : Yes (not really)<br><b>Mum</b> : I'm sure you're already feeling better right?<br><b>Anna</b> : I guess. So, [add some topic changer - You name it. Any word, really]<br><br>I love my mum. But yeah, that's kind of exhausting. And the magnesium. OMG, the magnesium. But reading about this kind of character? Hilarious. Mum, I'm writing a book about you (not really).<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437533383i/15595829._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Love interest? Adorable. Smile-inducing. I have no idea why I'm writing one-word sentences. I might be lazy. Major information : he write <i>notes</i>. End of story. <br><br>Just a thing : Linus? What's this name? I kept thinking "Linux" and that was just so <i>weird</i> *shakes head* <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437533383i/15595830._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>● I already stated that I loved when authors used <b>different writing formats</b> and lucky me! Kinsella does it all the time : messages, notes, movie script : I eat that stuff, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23305614.Finding_Audrey" title="Finding Audrey by Sophie Kinsella" rel="nofollow noopener"> Finding Audrey</a> was right up my alley. <br><br>● Oh, and - <b>the dialogues are fantastic and feel real</b>. Hilarious. I know, I have to stop using that word. Someday (not when I talk about Kinsella)<br><br>► <b>Let's have a little brainstorming okay?</b> (God. I hate that word. My fellow French use it all the freaking time for no reason. Hello, <i>remue-méninges</i>, you people) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437533383i/15595831._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That's it. Is that really a brainstorming? Fuck if I know (in fact I do. It's not. Not really. I mean. Who cares?) <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I think what I've realized is, life is all about climbing up, slipping down, and picking yourself up again. And it doesn't matter if you slip down. As long as you're kind of heading more or less upwards. That's all you can hope for. More or less upwards."</b>
</blockquote><br>Such a great journey to follow. <s>And sorry for the messy review but I did warn you didn't I?</s><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_1304021850" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1304021850" />
    <a title="Chantal " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31668723-chantal"><img alt="Chantal " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464626501p2/31668723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1304021850?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chantal " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chantal " href="/user/show/31668723-chantal">Chantal </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=listened-on-audio">listened-on-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=published-2015">published-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1304021850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5687349881317111688">There are two things I think we can all agree on when it comes to books dealing with mental health:<br/>1)	We want more of them because it is such an important issue and isn’t talked about enough<br/>2)	Mental health books will ALWAYS be polarizing<br/><br/>There are two reasons for the second point:<br/>a)	A book deals with the heavy issue in a very serious manner and appears to be quite “dark”<br/>b)	The author decides to take a more humorous approach and pairs a heavy topic such as mental health with a writing style and s</span>
  <span id="freeText5687349881317111688" style="display:none">There are two things I think we can all agree on when it comes to books dealing with mental health:<br />1)	We want more of them because it is such an important issue and isn’t talked about enough<br />2)	Mental health books will ALWAYS be polarizing<br /><br />There are two reasons for the second point:<br />a)	A book deals with the heavy issue in a very serious manner and appears to be quite “dark”<br />b)	The author decides to take a more humorous approach and pairs a heavy topic such as mental health with a writing style and story that is more fluffy<br /><br />Which of these you prefer completely depends on your personal interpretation of a book and your experience with the topic that the story is dealing with. In my opinion, both choices are equally valid, as long as the author stays respectful. <br /><br />In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23305614.Finding_Audrey" title="Finding Audrey by Sophie Kinsella" rel="nofollow noopener">Finding Audrey</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6160.Sophie_Kinsella" title="Sophie Kinsella" rel="nofollow noopener">Sophie Kinsella</a> chose to take route b and for me personally this worked very well. <b>I found the novel to be heartfelt and charming, at times funny, at others poignant and always honest. It is a feel-good novel that will make you laugh out loud; certainly fluffy and light but never offensive.</b> <br /><br />The story follows 14-year-old Audrey who suffers from severe social anxiety which results in her not being able to leave the house or interact with anyone outside of her immediate family. She constantly wears sunglasses (even inside her own house) because making eye contact with people triggers panic attacks. <br />Interestingly, it isn’t a story about bullying or what caused her to feel this way, but instead it focuses on healing and recovery. <br /><br /><b>All the characters in this novel were delightful.</b> Audrey’s family was so lovable and realistic, kind of crazy at times but that made them even more relatable. The family dynamics were extremely well done and Audrey was a great protagonist. Being inside her head was fun while still giving some insight into the thoughts of someone who is suffering from an anxiety disorder <br /><blockquote>“I’ve come to think of my lizard brain as basically a version of Felix. It’s totally random and makes no sense and you can’t let it run your life. If we let Felix run our lives, we’d all wear superhero costumes all day long and eat nothing but ice-cream. But if you try to fight Felix, all you get is wails and screams and tantrums, and it all gets more and more stressy. So the thing is to listen to him with half an ear and nod your head and then ignore him and do what you want to do. Same with the lizard brain.”</blockquote><br /><b>If you are looking for a novel that teaches you about anxiety disorders this is not it.</b> You will not learn a huge amount, but you will enjoy the ride. <br /><br /><b>There is a romance in here but fortunately it really takes the backseat.</b> It isn’t a book that tells us that you need a boyfriend/girlfriend to become healthy. Instead, Linus offers his friendship and supports Audrey but he certainly doesn’t solve all her problems. <br /><br />Another thing I loved about the novel was how well therapy and progress was portrayed. <b>It was a very therapy positive book and I loved how it was made clear that progress isn’t a straight line upwards, but instead you will have setbacks and it is up to you how you want to proceed from there.</b> <br /><br />I really enjoyed this novel and highly recommend it to everyone. It is a very quick and easy read that will leave you with a smile on your face. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5687349881317111688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7323703543330141654"> <b>3,5-4 STARS</b><br/><br/> What a sweet, funny and fast paced story! I loved the Shopaholic series,even thought I have read only the first three books I enjoyed all of them and I was excited to see a new book from her which was so different This is a young adult book where she covers sensitive subjects such as anxiety disorder, addiction with computers and bullying.<br/><br/>This story is about Audrey,a fifteen year old girl suffering from anxiety disorder after an experience of school bullying that has led her to goin</span>
  <span id="freeText7323703543330141654" style="display:none"> <b>3,5-4 STARS</b><br><br> What a sweet, funny and fast paced story! I loved the Shopaholic series,even thought I have read only the first three books I enjoyed all of them and I was excited to see a new book from her which was so different This is a young adult book where she covers sensitive subjects such as anxiety disorder, addiction with computers and bullying.<br><br>This story is about Audrey,a fifteen year old girl suffering from anxiety disorder after an experience of school bullying that has led her to going to therapy. Now she stays at home and interferes with her family and her therapist as she tries to regain her confidence! She will meet her brother's friend Linus a funny boy, who will help her live again.<br><br>Audrey the main character is cute and funny!I liked her and I felt sorry for her and what she had been through!There was a little bit of romance in this and it was sweet!I really liked Linus,I loved the messages he wrote with Aubrey they were cute and I like that he helped Audrey to overcome her anxiety.Her family is so unique and funny! I loved their hilarious interactions.<br><br>I truly enjoyed this book !I can’t wait to see more books in this genre from Sophie Kinsella!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432546650i/14980279.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Arc provided via Netgalley for an honest review!</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11903198562347922292">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to Penguin Random House UK Children’s and NetGalley.)<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“To put you out of your misery, here’s the full diagnosis. Social Anxiety Disorder, General Anxiety Disorder and Depressive Episodes. Episodes. Like depression is a sitcom with a fun punchline.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431261751i/14815293._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was a cute story a girl suffering from an anxiety disorder, and her crazy mother!<br/><br/>I liked Audrey in this story and I felt really sorry for her. What she h</span>
  <span id="freeText11903198562347922292" style="display:none">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to Penguin Random House UK Children’s and NetGalley.)<br><br><b>
  <i>“To put you out of your misery, here’s the full diagnosis. Social Anxiety Disorder, General Anxiety Disorder and Depressive Episodes. Episodes. Like depression is a sitcom with a fun punchline.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431261751i/14815293._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was a cute story a girl suffering from an anxiety disorder, and her crazy mother!<br><br>I liked Audrey in this story and I felt really sorry for her. What she had been through had obviously been traumatic, and being unable to even look at people without panicking was really limiting for her. <br><br><b>
  <i>“But I think it’s time, Audrey. I think you can do it. Call it project Starbucks.”<br>Starbucks? Is she kidding?<br>Tears have started to my eyes. My blood is pulsing in panic. I can’t go to Starbucks. I can’t.</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431261560i/14815263.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The storyline in this was really funny! Audrey’s mother was quite crazy about the possibility of Audrey’s brother Frank being addicted to video games, and went to ridiculous lengths to try and stop him from playing. I loved Audrey’s take on her mother’s addiction to The Daily Mail, and the way this book made me laugh!<br><br><b>
  <i>“I’ll do anything. I’ll stack the dishwasher. I’ll phone Grandma every night. I’ll…” He casts about wildly. “I’ll read to deaf people.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431261694i/14815284.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There was a little bit of romance in this, and it was quite sweet! I really liked Linus, and he really helped Audrey to overcome her anxiety.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Had to give you this before I go.” <br>For a few moments I don’t dare read it. But at last I open it up and stare at the words inside. My head is prickling all over with disbelief. My breath is jumpy as it read it. He wrote that. He wrote that. To me.<br>“It’s a kiss.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431261694ra/14815285.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending to this was pretty good, and I liked that we got a happy ending.<br>7 out of 10</span>

  <span id="freeText14652200462523469612" style="display:none"><b>"But what I've learned is not to <i>fight</i> my lizard brain, but kind of <i>tolerate</i> it. <div id="review_2586637682" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2586637682" />
    <a title="Harley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70067095-harley"><img alt="Harley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586871609p2/70067095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2586637682?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Harley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Harley" href="/user/show/70067095-harley">Harley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70067095-harley?shelf=1-and-1-5-stars">1-and-1-5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2586637682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13084169641340254022"><b>1 Star.</b><br/><br/>This is one of those books that I wish I could erase from my mind.<br/><br/>The only positive from this book is the anxiety representation which was <i>completely</i> ruined as the book continued by the way.<br/><br/>Firstly, the characters were majorly unoriginal and annoying. Audrey's brother Frank was a 'nerdy' teenager whose love was video games, their mum was unnecessarily dramatic and did my head in, their dad was practically non-existent and Linus, oh my, he was the <i>worst</i>. They all got on my nerves so much t</span>
  <span id="freeText13084169641340254022" style="display:none"><b>1 Star.</b><br /><br />This is one of those books that I wish I could erase from my mind.<br /><br />The only positive from this book is the anxiety representation which was <i>completely</i> ruined as the book continued by the way.<br /><br />Firstly, the characters were majorly unoriginal and annoying. Audrey's brother Frank was a 'nerdy' teenager whose love was video games, their mum was unnecessarily dramatic and did my head in, their dad was practically non-existent and Linus, oh my, he was the <i>worst</i>. They all got on my nerves so much that they made me want to throw my book across the room.<br /><br />And as if that wasn't annoying enough, the words 'like', 'whatever' and 'so' were <u>massively</u> overused, also along with abbreviations such as 'FFS' and 'OMG'. I've seen this before and I feel that authors just do this because they believe that it appeals to teenagers more and it is how everyone speaks but <i>no</i>, just <u>no</u>. It was annoying enough for me to want to stop reading <s>and I bloody wish that I did</s>. The writing itself too was just plain and undescriptive leaving me even more bored.<br /><br />However, the thing that got on my nerves the <u>most</u> was how Audrey's mental health was dealt with. Audrey has severe social anxiety to the point where she has to wear sunglasses all the time to avoid eye contact. This is a girl who can <i>barely</i> as little as make <i>eye</i> contact with people and suddenly she meets a <i>boy</i> (yes, it's always a boy isn't it?) and within a few minutes they are <i>kissing</i>. So she can't make eye contact with people but she can make out with Linus, a boy she barely knows? Okay, sure. But what was even <u>more</u> infuriating was that after she met Linus she magically wanted to get better and felt she was cured. Is this how mental health works now? You fall in 'love' and bam, you get better? Maybe I'm being harsh but that seems pretty unrealistic to me.<br /><br />So I had <u>many</u> issuses with this book, and I wouldn't recommend it at all if you want a raw representation of mental health. Go and read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18075234.Challenger_Deep" title="Challenger Deep by Neal Shusterman" rel="nofollow noopener">Challenger Deep</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16120760.The_Shock_of_the_Fall" title="The Shock of the Fall by Nathan Filer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shock of the Fall</a> instead.<br /><br />I never want to think about this book again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13084169641340254022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1100241728" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1100241728" />
    <a title="Christina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14066678-christina"><img alt="Christina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481826762p2/14066678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1100241728?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/14066678-christina">Christina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1100241728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17629137650685614177">4 stars!<br/><br/><i>
  <b>"We're just looking and looking at each other. And I can feel something new between us, something even more intimate than anything we've ever done. Eye to eye. It's the most powerful connection in the world."</b>
</i><br/><br/>This book just reminds me about how much I love Sophie Kinsella's standalone novel's. This book is about a 14 year old girl named Audrey, who after an unpleasant incident, develops an anxiety disorder. She's stopped going to her school, rarely leaves her house and wears dark glas</span>
  <span id="freeText17629137650685614177" style="display:none">4 stars!<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"We're just looking and looking at each other. And I can feel something new between us, something even more intimate than anything we've ever done. Eye to eye. It's the most powerful connection in the world."</b>
</i><br /><br />This book just reminds me about how much I love Sophie Kinsella's standalone novel's. This book is about a 14 year old girl named Audrey, who after an unpleasant incident, develops an anxiety disorder. She's stopped going to her school, rarely leaves her house and wears dark glasses as a way to protect herself. <br /><br /><b>"I know in my rational head that eyes are not frightening. They're tiny little harmless blobs of jelly. They're, like, a minuscule fraction of our whole body area. We all have them. So why should they bother me? But I've had a lot of time to think about this, and if you ask me, most people underestimate eyes. For a start, they're powerful. They have range. You can focus on someone a hundred feet away, through a whole bunch of people, and they <i>know</i> you're you're looking at them. What other bit of human anatomy can do that? It's practically being psychic is what it is. But they're like vortexes too. They're infinite. You look someone straight in the eye and your whole soul can be sucked out in a nanosecond. That's what it feels like. Other people's eyes are limitless and that's what scares me."</b><br /><br />She's on medication. She has regular visits with Dr. Sarah, who describes her progress as a graph chart, with a bit of a jagged line...a little up, a little down. As part of her treatment, Dr. Sarah has Audrey start filming a documentary. First just the things around her...then slowly working up to doing interviews, with the theory that maybe eye contact with someone through the camera would be easier. The book switches between dialogue and film transcripts. And it worked really well. <br />While Audrey was the MC, the book focused not just on her, but on her family and their ups and downs together as well. She has 2 brothers, an older one named Frank and a 4 year old named Felix. I both adored and was very annoyed by Audrey's parents. They made for some hilarious conversation.<br />Things really start to turn around for Audrey when she begins to have contact with Linus, Frank's friend who begins to come around the house often to play a video game with him. They eventually develop a relationship and Audrey finds that after some initial visits and awkward encounters, she can feel somewhat comfortable with him. She can talk through her fears with him and he gently challenges her to push her boundaries and comfort zone a bit. <br />I thought that Sophie Kinsella handled both the matter of Audreys disorder and the way people can react to it really well. A lot of people had misconceptions and thought Audrey was crazy because of her disorder, but of course that wasn't the case.<br /><br /><b>"Here's the full diagnosis : Social Anxiety Disorder, General Anxiety Disorder, and Depressive Episodes. <i>Episodes.</i> Like depression is a sitcom with a fun punch line each time. Or a TV box set loaded with cliffhangers. The only cliffhanger in my life is ' Will I ever get rid of this shit? ' and believe me, it gets pretty monotonous."</b><br /><br />The only thing I didn't like was that we never quite found out what happened to Audrey to spark all of this...there are little hints here and there and names mentioned, but no specific details are given, which just leaves you to use your imagination. But still, this is a very cute, but touching book. I really enjoyed going on Audrey's journey with her. <br /><br /><b>"But I'm sick of this bloody jagged graph," I said in frustration. "You know, two steps up, one step down. It's so <i>painful.</i> It's so <i>slow.</i> It's like this endless game of snakes and ladders."<br />And mum just looked at me as if she wanted to laugh or maybe cry, and she said, "But, Audrey, that's what life is. We're all on a jagged graph. I know I am. Up a bit, down a bit. That's life."</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17629137650685614177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1089545226" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1089545226" />
    <a title="Juhina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4311208-juhina"><img alt="Juhina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418856027p2/4311208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1089545226?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juhina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juhina" href="/user/show/4311208-juhina">Juhina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4311208-juhina?shelf=random-house">random-house</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4311208-juhina?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4311208-juhina?shelf=my-arcs">my-arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4311208-juhina?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1089545226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11656483886087958812">This was such a fun book! I honestly didn't expect any less from Sophie Kinsella but I was a bit hesitant because of two reasons, one being that this is her first try at writing middle grade books, and another being that I never really enjoy middle grade books. The first reason is that I really hoped Kinsella's humor will translate through such a young protagonist (and oh boy, did it ever!) and the other is that I often find MG characters too immature for my taste, but Kinsella's magic did it ag</span>
  <span id="freeText11656483886087958812" style="display:none">This was such a fun book! I honestly didn't expect any less from Sophie Kinsella but I was a bit hesitant because of two reasons, one being that this is her first try at writing middle grade books, and another being that I never really enjoy middle grade books. The first reason is that I really hoped Kinsella's humor will translate through such a young protagonist (and oh boy, did it ever!) and the other is that I often find MG characters too immature for my taste, but Kinsella's magic did it again and totally made this book and character relatable, fun, and all with an important message delivered to the readers. <br /><br />Anxiety disorders are actually more common than what we think. Unfortunately many people aren't aware of the actual clinical term and brush it off as a personality defect. Mental and psychological illnesses are unfortunately treated as a second class citizen in relation to physical illnesses. I really applaud and admire Kinsella for picking such an important topic and simplifying it and relating it to young teens. Audrey went through a traumatic event in her school that caused her to develop severe anxiety. She wears sunglasses at all times and now never leaves the house (she is in the middle of transferring to another school). <br /><br />The story isn't just Audrey's story, but it is her whole family's story. One thing Kinsella did brilliantly is the family dynamic and relationship. Audrey's older and younger brothers will remind you of your own siblings. Her mother worries constantly and her dad backs her up in the parenting department just to keep the peace. We all have the bad cop good cop labels for our parents right? I just liked how relatable the whole family dynamic was. Also, A Kinsella book isn't one if it isn't laugh out loud funny, which Finding Audrey totally is. Her brother plays an online RPG game that he's preparing with his friends to enter a global tournament.. and that requires countless hours of playing, something that has turned red flags for their mom... and commence the crazy acts, from finding inventive ways to get around the ban from playing, to restoring to the most extreme actions, like his mom throwing a €1,100 laptop out the window to finally get her son's attention (This isn't the spoiler, the book opens up with this exact scene). If I could choose one word to describe Finding Audrey, it would be fun. I can't wait for Sophie Kinsella to venture more into the non adult world (YA book next? please?), as well as more adult books. Basically I will read anything Sophie Kinsella writes. I definitely recommend it to all Sophie Kinsella fans as well as readers who want to try her writing but aren't interested (yet) in her adult books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11656483886087958812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('K+W23bxcsxTpI4djSLZ+UryHMkY4d5duG6ga9rL8NHARw98PBwJ6fE4IMwK/Q3SNatjVjvb6GQlA1lxHf7/G6g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0PEBzll+8F1wF+7bDYcKQivbqQ3L2SdColtS6C6w05Lq12gc4iA5Ndc8Wrr6cgCd/YROxQVUqSX5JRRZ4/MhCA==')})
  }
//]]>

Worst of all, she’s forcing Olive to spend the day with her sworn enemy, Ethan, who just happens to be the best man.\n\nOlive braces herself to get through 24 hours of wedding hell before she can return to her comfortable, unlucky life. But when the entire wedding party gets food poisoning from eating bad shellfish, the only people who aren’t affected are Olive and Ethan. And now there’s an all-expenses-paid honeymoon in Hawaii up for grabs.\n\nPutting their mutual hatred aside for the sake of a free vacation, Olive and Ethan head for paradise, determined to avoid each other at all costs. But when Olive runs into her future boss, the little white lie she tells him is suddenly at risk to become a whole lot bigger. She and Ethan now have to pretend to be loving newlyweds, and her luck seems worse than ever. But the weird thing is that she doesn’t mind playing pretend. In fact, she feels kind of... lucky.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11759032907993294298\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/6160.Sophie_Kinsella">About Sophie Kinsella</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/6160.Sophie_Kinsella"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1245821549p3/6160.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/6160.Sophie_Kinsella">Sophie Kinsella
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15947555208113984716">Sophie Kinsella has sold over 40 million copies of her books in more than 60 countries, and she has been translated into over 40 languages.<br/><br/>Sophie Kinsella first hit the UK bestseller lists in September 2000 with her first novel in the Shopaholic series – The Secret Dreamworld of a Shopaholic (also published as Confessions of a Shopaholic). The book’s heroine, Becky Bloomwood – a fun and feisty fin</span>
  <span id="freeText15947555208113984716" style="display:none">Sophie Kinsella has sold over 40 million copies of her books in more than 60 countries, and she has been translated into over 40 languages.<br /><br />Sophie Kinsella first hit the UK bestseller lists in September 2000 with her first novel in the Shopaholic series – The Secret Dreamworld of a Shopaholic (also published as Confessions of a Shopaholic). The book’s heroine, Becky Bloomwood – a fun and feisty financial journalist who loves shopping but is hopeless with money – captured the hearts of readers worldwide. Becky has since featured in seven further bestselling books, Shopaholic Abroad (also published as Shopaholic Takes Manhattan), Shopaholic Ties the Knot, Shopaholic &amp; Sister, Shopaholic &amp; Baby, Mini Shopaholic, Shopaholic to the Stars and Shopaholic to the Rescue. Becky Bloomwood came to the big screen in 2009 with the hit Disney movie Confessions of a Shopaholic, starring Isla Fisher and Hugh Dancy.<br /><br />Sophie has also written seven standalone novels which have all been bestsellers in the UK, USA and other countries around the world: Can You Keep A Secret?, The Undomestic Goddess, Remember Me?, Twenties Girl, I’ve Got Your Number, Wedding Night, and My Not So Perfect Life, which was a Goodreads Choice Awards finalist for Best Fiction in 2017. <br /><br />In 2014 she published a Young Adult novel Finding Audrey about a teenage girl with social anxiety and her madcap family, and in January 2018, Sophie published her first illustrated book for young readers about the charming adventures of a mother-daughter fairy duo, Mummy Fairy and Me (also published as Fairy Mom and Me).<br /><br />Sophie’s latest novel, Surprise Me, published in February 2018, presents a humorous yet moving portrait of a marriage—its intricacies, comforts, and complications. Surprise Me reveals that hidden layers in a close relationship are often yet to be discovered.<br /><br />Sophie wrote her first novel under her real name, Madeleine Wickham, at the tender age of 24, whilst she was working as a financial journalist. The Tennis Party was immediately hailed as a success by critics and the public alike and became a top ten bestseller. She went on to publish six more novels as Madeleine Wickham: A Desirable Residence, Swimming Pool Sunday, The Gatecrasher, The Wedding Girl, Cocktails for Three and Sleeping Arrangements.<br /><br />Sophie was born in London. She studied music at New College, Oxford, but after a year switched to Politics, Philosophy and Economics. She now lives in London, UK, with her husband and family.<br /><br /><br />Visit Sophie's Facebook page: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/SophieKinsellaOfficial">http://www.facebook.com/SophieKinsell...</a><br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/45600-shopaholic" rel="nofollow noopener">Shopaholic</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15947555208113984716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
